## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task describes the rate of change of concentration over time in a chemical reaction, indicating it belongs to the scientific domain of chemical kinetics. The possible physical relationships between variables involve reaction rates, concentrations, and time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA/dt = c0 (constant rate of disappearance)
- First-order reaction: dA/dt = c0 * A (rate of disappearance is proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA/dt = c0 * A**2 (rate of disappearance is proportional to square of concentration)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA/dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: dA/dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal rate-response)
- Power-law scaling: dA/dt = c0 * t**c1 (scale-free scaling relationship between rate and time)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: dA/dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Lumped-parameter models: dA/dt = c0 * A + c1 (representing a simplified chemical reaction process)
- Lumped parameter reaction kinetics with linear wall deposition rate: dA/dt = c0*A +c1*t (effect of wall deposition in a reaction chamber)
- Simple ordinary differential equation: dA/dt = c0 + c1 * t (a simple expression relating rate of change to time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Dependence on a single variable → Simple power-law scaling: dA/dt = c0 * A**c1
- Dependence on time → Time-dependent terms: dA/dt = c0 * t**c1, dA/dt = c0 + c1 * t
- Dependence on concentration → Saturation/clipping effects: dA/dt = c0 * A / (A + c1), dA/dt = c0 * A**2 / (A**2 + c1)
- Absorption isotherm → Langmuir adsorption isotherm: dA/dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A)
- Adsorption on heterogeneous surface → Freundlich isotherm: dA/dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Autocatalytic reactions → Exponential growth: dA/dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t)
- Thermal activation → Arrhenius-like: dA/dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t)
